<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Napoleon</span></h1>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Military leader and emperor of France</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about Napoleon I. </p>

<div style="line-height:0;margin-bottom:-2px;">​</div> <div style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:1px;">​</div>(<abbr title="married">m.</abbr> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1038841319" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="rt-commentedText tooltip" title="11 March 1810">1810</span>)<wbr/>​</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Issue<br/><span style="font-weight:normal"><i><a href="#Wives,_mistresses,_and_children">Detail</a></i></span></th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_II" title="Napoleon II">Napoleon II</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_L%C3%A9on" title="Charles Léon">Charles Léon</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Colonna-Walewski" title="Alexandre Colonna-Walewski">Alexandre Colonna-Walewski</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/%C3%89milie_Pellapra" title="Émilie Pellapra">Émilie Pellapra</a> (?)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox" style="border-collapse:collapse; <div class="thumbinner" style="width:275px">
<div class="center" style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Military career of Napoleon Bonaparte">Battles of Napoleon</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1111531371">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output div.mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" data-graph-id="7d33a994b3730e0709b833934e95470bf3d93b74" style="min-width:273px;min-height:240px"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="font-size:75%"><a class="mw-kartographer-maplink" data-lat="45.3" data-lon="13" data-mw="interface" data-overlays='["_9ac9b4f2d9036e0c398d66bd8e167e058ec27706"]' data-style="osm-intl" data-zoom="4" href="/wiki/Special:Map/4/45.3/13/en">[Interactive fullscreen map]</a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">Rescale the fullscreen map to see Saint Helena</div>
</div></div>
<p><b>Napoleon</b>, also <b>Napoleon Bonaparte</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[a]</a></sup> (born <b>Napoleone Buonaparte</b>; 15 August 1769 – 5 May 1821), and later known by his <a href="/wiki/Regnal_name" title="Regnal name">regnal name</a> <b>Napoleon I</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[b]</a></sup> was a French military and political leader who rose to prominence during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> and led <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Military career of Napoleon Bonaparte">several successful campaigns</a> during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">Revolutionary Wars</a>. He was the <i>de facto</i> leader of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" title="First French Republic">French Republic</a> as First Consul from 1799 to 1804, and as Napoleon I, he was <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_the_French" title="Emperor of the French">Emperor of the French</a> from 1804 until 1814 and again in <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days" title="Hundred Days">1815</a>. Napoleon's political and cultural legacy has endured to this day, and he stands as one of the most celebrated and controversial leaders in world history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts,_Andrew_2014_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts,_Andrew_2014-4">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon was born on the island of <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, not long after its <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Corsica" title="French conquest of Corsica">annexation by France</a>, to a native family descending from minor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_nobility" title="Italian nobility">Italian nobility</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis-7">[5]</a></sup> He supported the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> in 1789 while serving in the French army, and tried to spread its ideals to his native Corsica. He rose rapidly in the Army after he saved the governing <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">French Directory</a> by <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">firing on royalist insurgents</a>. In 1796, he began <a href="/wiki/Italian_campaigns_of_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars">a military campaign</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrians</a> and their Italian allies, scoring decisive victories and becoming a national hero. Two years later, he led a <a href="/wiki/French_campaign_in_Egypt_and_Syria" title="French campaign in Egypt and Syria">military expedition to Egypt</a> that served as a springboard to political power. He engineered a <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">coup in November 1799</a> and became <i><a href="/wiki/French_Consulate" title="French Consulate">First Consul</a> of the Republic</i>. Differences with the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> meant that the French faced the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</a> by 1805. Napoleon shattered this coalition with victories in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Campaign</a>, and at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, which led to the dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. In 1806, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition" title="War of the Fourth Coalition">Fourth Coalition</a> took up arms against him because <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> became worried about growing French influence on the continent. Napoleon defeated Prussia at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena%E2%80%93Auerstedt" title="Battle of Jena–Auerstedt">battles of Jena and Auerstedt</a>, marched the <a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Armée">Grande Armée</a> into <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, and defeated <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">the Russians</a> in June 1807 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Friedland" title="Battle of Friedland">Friedland</a>, forcing the defeated nations of the Fourth Coalition to accept the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a>. Two years later, the Austrians challenged the French again during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition" title="War of the Fifth Coalition">War of the Fifth Coalition</a>, but Napoleon solidified his grip over Europe after triumphing at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a>.
</p><p>Hoping to extend the <a href="/wiki/Continental_System" title="Continental System">Continental System</a>, his embargo against Britain, Napoleon invaded the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> and declared his brother <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a> the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King of Spain</a> in 1808. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">The Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">the Portuguese</a> revolted in the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a>, culminating in defeat for Napoleon's marshals. Napoleon launched an <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">invasion of Russia</a> in the summer of 1812. The resulting campaign witnessed the catastrophic retreat of Napoleon's <a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Armée">Grande Armée</a>. In 1813, Prussia and Austria joined Russian forces in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sixth_Coalition" title="Sixth Coalition">Sixth Coalition</a> against France. A chaotic military campaign resulted in a large coalition army defeating Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a> in October 1813. The coalition <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1814_campaign_in_France" title="1814 campaign in France">invaded France</a> and captured Paris, forcing Napoleon to abdicate in April 1814. He was exiled to the island of <a href="/wiki/Elba" title="Elba">Elba</a>, between Corsica and Italy. In France, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourbon_dynasty" title="Bourbon dynasty">Bourbons</a> were <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Restoration_in_France" title="Bourbon Restoration in France">restored to power</a>. However, Napoleon escaped Elba in February 1815 and took control of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup> The Allies responded by forming a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Seventh_Coalition" title="War of the Seventh Coalition">Seventh Coalition</a>, which defeated Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> in June 1815. The British exiled him to the remote island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>, where he died in 1821 at the age of 51. Napoleon had an extensive impact on the modern world, bringing liberal reforms to the many countries he conquered, especially the regions of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">modern Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. He implemented many liberal policies in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[c]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg"><img alt="Half-length portrait of a wigged middle-aged man with a well-to-do jacket. His left hand is tucked inside his waistcoat." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1786" data-file-width="1378" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/170px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/255px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/340px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon's father, <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Buonaparte" title="Carlo Buonaparte">Carlo Buonaparte</a>, fought for <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsican</a> independence under <a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Paoli" title="Pasquale Paoli">Pasquale Paoli</a>, but after their defeat he eventually became the island's representative to the court of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Napoleon's family was of <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> origin. His paternal ancestors, the Buonapartes, descended from a minor <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscan</a> noble family who emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> in the 16th century and his maternal ancestors, the Ramolinos, descended from a minor <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> noble family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup> The Buonapartes were also the relatives, by marriage and by birth, of the Pietrasentas, Costas, Paraviccinis, and Bonellis, all <a href="/wiki/Corsicans" title="Corsicans">Corsican</a> families of the interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> His parents <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Buonaparte" title="Carlo Buonaparte">Carlo Maria di Buonaparte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Letizia_Bonaparte" title="Letizia Bonaparte">Maria Letizia Ramolino</a> maintained an ancestral home called "<a href="/wiki/Maison_Bonaparte" title="Maison Bonaparte">Casa Buonaparte</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Ajaccio" title="Ajaccio">Ajaccio</a>. It was there, at this home, that Napoleon was born, on 15 August 1769. He was the fourth child and third son of the family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[d]</a></sup> He had an elder brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a>, and younger siblings <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Bonaparte" title="Lucien Bonaparte">Lucien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elisa_Bonaparte" title="Elisa Bonaparte">Elisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bonaparte" title="Louis Bonaparte">Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Bonaparte" title="Pauline Bonaparte">Pauline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Bonaparte" title="Caroline Bonaparte">Caroline</a>, and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Bonaparte" title="Jérôme Bonaparte">Jérôme</a>. Napoleon was baptised as a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, under the name <i><a href="/wiki/Napoleone" title="Napoleone">Napoleone</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-:22-19">[15]</a></sup> In his youth, his name was also spelled as <i>Nabulione</i>, <i>Nabulio</i>, <i>Napolionne</i>, and <i>Napulione</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwyerxv_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-dwyerxv-20">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon was born in the same year that the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> (former Italian state) ceded the region of Corsica to France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-21">[17]</a></sup> The state sold <a href="/wiki/Westphalian_sovereignty" title="Westphalian sovereignty">sovereign rights</a> a year before his birth and the <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Corsica" title="French conquest of Corsica">island was conquered</a> by France during the year of his birth. It was formally incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_France" title="Provinces of France">province</a> in 1770, after <a href="/wiki/History_of_Corsica#Renaissance" title="History of Corsica">500 years under Genoese rule</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corsican_Republic" title="Corsican Republic">14 years of independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[e]</a></sup> Napoleon's parents joined the Corsican resistance and fought against the French to maintain independence, even when Maria was pregnant with him. His father Carlo was an attorney who had supported and actively collaborated with patriot <a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Paoli" title="Pasquale Paoli">Pasquale Paoli</a> during the Corsican war of independence against France;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis-7">[5]</a></sup> after the Corsican defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ponte_Novu" title="Battle of Ponte Novu">Ponte Novu</a> in 1769 and Paoli's exile in Britain, Carlo began working for the new French government and went on to be named representative of the island to the court of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI</a> in 1777.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-26">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The dominant influence of Napoleon's childhood was his mother, whose firm discipline restrained a rambunctious child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-26">[21]</a></sup> Later in life, Napoleon stated, "The future destiny of the child is always the work of the mother."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[22]</a></sup> Napoleon's maternal grandmother had married into the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Faesch" title="Faesch">Fesch</a> family in her second marriage, and Napoleon's uncle, the cardinal <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fesch" title="Joseph Fesch">Joseph Fesch</a>, would fulfill a role as protector of the Bonaparte family for some years. Napoleon's noble, moderately affluent background afforded him greater opportunities to study than were available to a typical Corsican of the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="3744" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg/220px-Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg/330px-Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg/440px-Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_%C3%A9colier_IMG_6712.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue of Napoleon as a schoolboy in Brienne, aged 15, by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Louis_Rochet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Louis Rochet (page does not exist)">Louis Rochet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Rochet" title="fr:Louis Rochet">fr</a>]</span> (1853)</div></div></div>
<p>When he turned 9 years old,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[25]</a></sup> he moved to <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">the French mainland</a> and enrolled at a religious school in <a href="/wiki/Autun" title="Autun">Autun</a> in January 1779. In May, he transferred with a scholarship to a <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brienne-le-Ch%C3%A2teau" title="Brienne-le-Château">Brienne-le-Château</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxvi_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-31">[26]</a></sup> In his youth he was an outspoken <a href="/wiki/Corsican_nationalism" title="Corsican nationalism">Corsican nationalist</a> and supported the state's independence from France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-32">[27]</a></sup> Like many Corsicans, Napoleon spoke and read <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">Corsican</a> (as his mother tongue) and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> (as the official language of Corsica).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2014_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2014-33">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-32">[27]</a></sup> He began learning <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> in school at around age 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts201411_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts201411-36">[31]</a></sup> Although he became fluent in French, he spoke with a distinctive Corsican accent and never learned how to spell correctly in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[32]</a></sup> Consequently, Napoleon was treated unfairly by his schoolmates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-32">[27]</a></sup> He was, however, not an isolated case, as it was estimated in 1790 that fewer than 3 million people, out of France's population of 28 million, were able to speak standard French, and those who could write it were even fewer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon was routinely bullied by his peers for his accent, birthplace, short stature, mannerisms and inability to speak French quickly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34">[29]</a></sup> He became reserved and melancholy, applying himself to reading. An examiner observed that Napoleon "has always been distinguished for his application in mathematics. He is fairly well acquainted with history and geography ... This boy would make an excellent sailor".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[f]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>One story told of Napoleon at the school is that he led junior students to victory against senior students in a snowball fight, showing his leadership abilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler197312–14_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler197312–14-42">[36]</a></sup> In early adulthood, Napoleon briefly intended to become a writer; he authored a history of Corsica and a romantic <a href="/wiki/Novella" title="Novella">novella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>On completion of his studies at Brienne in 1784, Napoleon was admitted to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Militaire" title="École Militaire">École Militaire</a></i> in Paris. He trained to become an artillery officer and, when his father's death reduced his income, was forced to complete the two-year course in one year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwyer42_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-dwyer42-43">[37]</a></sup> He was the first Corsican to graduate from the <i>École Militaire</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwyer42_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-dwyer42-43">[37]</a></sup> He was examined by the famed scientist <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre-Simon Laplace">Pierre-Simon Laplace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_-_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="841" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/170px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/255px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/340px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_-_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon Bonaparte, aged 23, as lieutenant-colonel of a battalion of Corsican <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(France)" title="National Guard (France)">Republican volunteers</a>. Portrait by <a href="/wiki/Henri_F%C3%A9lix_Emmanuel_Philippoteaux" title="Henri Félix Emmanuel Philippoteaux">Henri Félix Emmanuel Philippoteaux</a></div></div></div>
<p>Upon graduating in September 1785, Bonaparte was <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">commissioned</a> a <a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a> in <a href="/wiki/1st_Artillery_Regiment_(France)" title="1st Artillery Regiment (France)"><i>La Fère</i> artillery regiment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[g]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxvi_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-31">[26]</a></sup> He served in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valence_(city)" title="Valence (city)">Valence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auxonne" title="Auxonne">Auxonne</a> until after the outbreak of the French Revolution in 1789. The young man still was a fervent Corsican nationalist during this period<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertsCh1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertsCh1-47">[40]</a></sup> and asked for leave to join his mentor <a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Paoli" title="Pasquale Paoli">Pasquale Paoli</a>, when the latter was allowed to return to Corsica by the National Assembly. Paoli had no sympathy for Napoleon, however, as he deemed his father a traitor for having deserted his cause for Corsican independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertsCh2_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertsCh2-48">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>He spent the early years of the Revolution in Corsica, fighting in a complex three-way struggle among royalists, revolutionaries, and Corsican nationalists. Napoleon, however, came to embrace the ideals of the Revolution, becoming a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Jacobin" title="Jacobin">Jacobins</a> and joining the pro-French Corsican Republicans who opposed Paoli's policy and his aspirations of secession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[42]</a></sup> He was given command over a battalion of volunteers and was promoted to captain in the regular army in July 1792, despite exceeding his leave of absence and leading a riot against French troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[43]</a></sup> When Corsica declared formal secession from France and requested the protection of the British government Napoleon and his commitment to the French Revolution came into conflict with Paoli, who had decided to sabotage the Corsican contribution to the <i><a href="/wiki/French_expedition_to_Sardinia" title="French expedition to Sardinia">Expédition de Sardaigne</a></i>, by preventing a French assault on the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Sardinian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/La_Maddalena" title="La Maddalena">La Maddalena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[44]</a></sup> Bonaparte and his family were compelled to flee to Toulon on the French mainland in June 1793 because of the split with Paoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxviii_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-52">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although he was born "Napoleone Buonaparte", it was after this that Napoleon began styling himself "Napoléon Bonaparte" but his family did not drop the name Buonaparte until 1796. The first known record of him signing his name as Bonaparte was at the age of 27 (in 1796).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-53">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-:22-19">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Siege_of_Toulon">Siege of Toulon</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Toulon" title="Siege of Toulon">Siege of Toulon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="795" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/170px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/255px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/340px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonaparte at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Toulon" title="Siege of Toulon">Siege of Toulon</a></div></div></div>
<p>In July 1793, Bonaparte published a pro-republican pamphlet entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Le_souper_de_Beaucaire" title="Le souper de Beaucaire">Le souper de Beaucaire</a></i> (Supper at <a href="/wiki/Beaucaire,_Gard" title="Beaucaire, Gard">Beaucaire</a>) which gained him the support of <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Robespierre" title="Augustin Robespierre">Augustin Robespierre</a>, younger brother of the Revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Maximilien_Robespierre" title="Maximilien Robespierre">Maximilien Robespierre</a>. With the help of his fellow Corsican <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Christophe_Saliceti" title="Antoine Christophe Saliceti">Antoine Christophe Saliceti</a>, Bonaparte was appointed senior gunner and artillery commander of the republican forces which arrived on 8 September at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>He adopted a plan to capture a hill where republican guns could dominate the city's harbour and force the British to evacuate. The assault on the position led to the capture of the city, but during it Bonaparte was wounded in the thigh on 16 December. Catching the attention of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Public_Safety" title="Committee of Public Safety">Committee of Public Safety</a>, he was put in charge of the artillery of France's <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Italy_(France)" title="Army of Italy (France)">Army of Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[50]</a></sup> On 22 December he was on his way to his new post in <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>, promoted from the rank of colonel to <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general" title="Brigadier general">brigadier general</a> at the age of 24. He devised plans for attacking the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a> as part of France's campaign <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">against the First Coalition</a>.
</p><p>The French army carried out Bonaparte's plan in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Saorgio_(1794)" title="Second Battle of Saorgio (1794)">Battle of Saorgio</a> in April 1794, and then advanced to seize <a href="/wiki/Ormea" title="Ormea">Ormea</a> in the mountains. From Ormea, they headed west to outflank the Austro-Sardinian positions around <a href="/wiki/Saorge" title="Saorge">Saorge</a>. After this campaign, Augustin Robespierre sent Bonaparte on a mission to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> to determine that country's intentions towards France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="13_Vend.C3.A9miaire"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="13_Vendémiaire">13 Vendémiaire</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">13 Vendémiaire</a></div>
<p>Some contemporaries alleged that Bonaparte was put under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> at <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> for his association with the Robespierres following their fall in the <a href="/wiki/Thermidorian_Reaction" title="Thermidorian Reaction">Thermidorian Reaction</a> in July 1794, but Napoleon's secretary <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_Fauvelet_de_Bourrienne" title="Louis Antoine Fauvelet de Bourrienne">Bourrienne</a> disputed the allegation in his memoirs. According to Bourrienne, jealousy was responsible, between the Army of the Alps and the Army of Italy (with whom Napoleon was seconded at the time).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[52]</a></sup> Bonaparte dispatched an impassioned defence in a letter to the commissar Saliceti, and he was subsequently acquitted of any wrongdoing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[53]</a></sup> He was released within two weeks (on 20 August) and, due to his technical skills, was asked to draw up plans to attack Italian positions in the context of France's war with Austria. He also took part in an expedition to take back Corsica from the British, but the French were repulsed by the British Royal Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1795, Bonaparte had become engaged to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9e_Clary" title="Désirée Clary">Désirée Clary</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Clary" title="François Clary">François Clary</a>. Désirée's sister <a href="/wiki/Julie_Clary" title="Julie Clary">Julie Clary</a> had married Bonaparte's elder brother Joseph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[55]</a></sup> In April 1795, he was assigned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Army_of_the_West_(1793)" title="Army of the West (1793)">Army of the West</a>, which was engaged in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e" title="War in the Vendée">War in the Vendée</a>—a civil war and royalist <a href="/wiki/Counter-revolutionary" title="Counter-revolutionary">counter-revolution</a> in Vendée, a region in west-central France on the Atlantic Ocean. As an infantry command, it was a demotion from artillery general—for which the army already had a full quota—and he pleaded poor health to avoid the posting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg"><img alt="Etching of a street, there are many pockets of smoke due to a group of republican artillery firing on royalists across the street at the entrance to a building" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="875" data-file-width="1418" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/220px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/330px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/440px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Journée du <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">13 Vendémiaire</a></i>, artillery fire in front of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint-Roch,_Paris" title="Church of Saint-Roch, Paris">Church of Saint-Roch, Paris</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rue_Saint-Honor%C3%A9" title="Rue Saint-Honoré">Rue Saint-Honoré</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>He was moved to the Bureau of <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">Topography</a> of the Committee of Public Safety and sought unsuccessfully to be transferred to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> in order to offer his services to the <a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Sultan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[57]</a></sup> During this period, he wrote the romantic novella <i><a href="/wiki/Clisson_et_Eug%C3%A9nie" title="Clisson et Eugénie">Clisson et Eugénie</a></i>, about a soldier and his lover, in a clear parallel to Bonaparte's own relationship with Désirée.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[58]</a></sup> On 15 September, Bonaparte was removed from the list of generals in regular service for his refusal to serve in the Vendée campaign. He faced a difficult financial situation and reduced career prospects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 October, royalists in Paris declared a rebellion against the <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m96_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-m96-67">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barras" title="Paul Barras">Paul Barras</a>, a leader of the Thermidorian Reaction, knew of Bonaparte's military exploits at Toulon and gave him command of the improvised forces in defence of the convention in the <a href="/wiki/Tuileries_Palace" title="Tuileries Palace">Tuileries Palace</a>. Napoleon had seen the <a href="/wiki/Insurrection_of_10_August_1792#Assault_on_the_Tuileries" title="Insurrection of 10 August 1792">massacre of the King's Swiss Guard</a> there three years earlier and realized that artillery would be the key to its defence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxvi_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-31">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>He ordered a young cavalry officer named <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Joachim Murat</a> to seize large <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannons</a> and used them to repel the attackers on 5 October 1795—<i>13 Vendémiaire An IV</i> in the <a href="/wiki/French_Republican_calendar" title="French Republican calendar">French Republican Calendar</a>; 1,400 royalists died and the rest fled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m96_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-m96-67">[60]</a></sup> He had cleared the streets with "a whiff of <a href="/wiki/Grapeshot" title="Grapeshot">grapeshot</a>", according to 19th-century historian <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Carlyle" title="Thomas Carlyle">Thomas Carlyle</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_French_Revolution:_A_History" title="The French Revolution: A History">The French Revolution: A History</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>The defeat of the royalist insurrection extinguished the threat to the Convention and earned Bonaparte sudden fame, wealth, and the patronage of the new government, the <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">Directory</a>. Murat married one of Napoleon's sisters, becoming his brother-in-law; he also served under Napoleon as one of his generals. Bonaparte was promoted to Commander of the Interior and given command of the Army of Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxviii_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-52">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Within weeks, he was romantically involved with <a href="/wiki/Empress_Jos%C3%A9phine" title="Empress Joséphine">Joséphine de Beauharnais</a>, the former mistress of Barras. The couple married on 9 March 1796 in a civil ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Italian_campaign">First Italian campaign</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italian_campaigns_of_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars">Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg"><img alt="A three-quarter-length depiction of Bonaparte, with black tunic and leather gloves, holding a standard and sword, turning backwards to look at his troops" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1926" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/170px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/255px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/340px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte_at_the_Pont_d%27Arcole" title="Bonaparte at the Pont d'Arcole">Bonaparte at the Pont d'Arcole</a></i>, by Baron <a href="/wiki/Antoine-Jean_Gros" title="Antoine-Jean Gros">Antoine-Jean Gros</a>, (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1801</span>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_du_Louvre" title="Musée du Louvre">Musée du Louvre</a>, Paris</div></div></div>
<p>Two days after the marriage, Bonaparte left <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> to take command of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Italy_(France)" title="Army of Italy (France)">Army of Italy</a>. He immediately went on the offensive, hoping to defeat the forces of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Piedmont</a> before their Austrian allies could intervene. In a series of rapid victories during the <a href="/wiki/Montenotte_campaign" title="Montenotte campaign">Montenotte Campaign</a>, he knocked Piedmont out of the war in two weeks. The French then focused on the Austrians for the remainder of the war, the highlight of which became the protracted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Mantua_(1796%E2%80%9397)" title="Siege of Mantua (1796–97)">struggle for Mantua</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrians</a> launched a series of offensives against the French to break the siege, but Napoleon defeated every relief effort, scoring victories at the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castiglione" title="Battle of Castiglione">Castiglione</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bassano" title="Battle of Bassano">Bassano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arcole" title="Battle of Arcole">Arcole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rivoli" title="Battle of Rivoli">Rivoli</a>. The decisive French triumph at Rivoli in January 1797 led to the collapse of the Austrian position in Italy. At Rivoli, the Austrians lost up to 14,000 men while the French lost about 5,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell201529_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell201529-71">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>The next phase of the campaign featured the French invasion of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> heartlands. French forces in Southern Germany had been defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Charles,_Duke_of_Teschen" title="Archduke Charles, Duke of Teschen">Archduke Charles</a> in 1796, but the Archduke withdrew his forces to protect <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> after learning about Napoleon's assault. In the first encounter between the two commanders, Napoleon pushed back his opponent and advanced deep into Austrian territory after winning at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarvis_(1797)" title="Battle of Tarvis (1797)">Battle of Tarvis</a> in March 1797. The Austrians were alarmed by the French thrust that reached all the way to <a href="/wiki/Leoben" title="Leoben">Leoben</a>, about 100 km from Vienna, and finally decided to sue for peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[65]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Leoben" title="Treaty of Leoben">Treaty of Leoben</a>, followed by the more comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Treaty of Campo Formio</a>, gave France control of most of northern Italy and the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, and a secret clause promised the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> to Austria. Bonaparte marched on Venice and <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Republic_of_Venice#12_May_1797:_the_Fall_of_the_Venetian_Republic" title="Fall of the Republic of Venice">forced its surrender</a>, ending 1,100 years of Venetian independence. He also authorized the French to loot treasures such as the <a href="/wiki/Horses_of_Saint_Mark" title="Horses of Saint Mark">Horses of Saint Mark</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[66]</a></sup>
On the journey, Bonaparte conversed much about the warriors of antiquity, especially <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Caesar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Africanus" title="Scipio Africanus">Scipio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a>. He studied their strategy and combined it with his own. In a question from Bourrienne, asking whether he gave his preference to Alexander or Caesar, Napoleon said that he places Alexander the Great in the first rank, the main reason being his campaign on Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille,_1797.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1195" data-file-width="1866" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg/220px-Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg/330px-Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg/440px-Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille%2C_1797.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_re%C3%A7oit_les_prisonniers_sur_le_champ_de_bataille,_1797.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonaparte during the Italian campaign in 1797</div></div></div>
<p>His application of conventional military ideas to real-world situations enabled his military triumphs, such as creative use of artillery as a mobile force to support his infantry. He stated later in life:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> "I have fought sixty battles and I have learned nothing which I did not know at the beginning. Look at Caesar; he fought the first like the last".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonaparte could win battles by concealment of troop deployments and concentration of his forces on the "hinge" of an enemy's weakened front. If he could not use his favourite <a href="/wiki/Pincer_movement" title="Pincer movement">envelopment strategy</a>, he would take up the central position and attack two co-operating forces at their hinge, swing round to fight one until it fled, then turn to face the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[69]</a></sup> In this Italian campaign, Bonaparte's army captured 150,000 prisoners, 540 cannons, and 170 <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">standards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[70]</a></sup> The French army fought 67 actions and won 18 <a href="/wiki/Pitched_battle" title="Pitched battle">pitched battles</a> through superior artillery technology and Bonaparte's tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the campaign, Bonaparte became increasingly influential in French politics. He founded two newspapers: one for the troops in his army and another for circulation in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[72]</a></sup> The royalists attacked Bonaparte for looting Italy and warned that he might become a dictator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[73]</a></sup> Napoleon's forces extracted an estimated $45 million in funds from Italy during their campaign there, another $12 million in precious metals and jewels. His forces also confiscated more than 300 priceless paintings and sculptures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell201530_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell201530-81">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonaparte sent General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pierre_Augereau" title="Pierre Augereau">Pierre Augereau</a> to Paris to lead a <i><a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a></i> and purge the royalists on 4 September—<a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Fructidor" title="Coup of 18 Fructidor">Coup of 18 Fructidor</a>. This left Barras and his Republican allies in control again but dependent on Bonaparte, who proceeded to peace negotiations with Austria. These negotiations resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Treaty of Campo Formio</a>, and Bonaparte returned to Paris in December as a hero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[75]</a></sup> He met <a href="/wiki/Charles_Maurice_de_Talleyrand-P%C3%A9rigord" title="Charles Maurice de Talleyrand-Périgord">Talleyrand</a>, France's new Foreign Minister—who served in the same capacity for Emperor Napoleon—and they began to prepare for an invasion of Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxviii_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-52">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_expedition">Egyptian expedition</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_campaign_in_Egypt_and_Syria" title="French campaign in Egypt and Syria">French campaign in Egypt and Syria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge,_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg"><img alt="Person on a horse looks towards a giant statue of a head in the desert, with a blue sky" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1838" data-file-width="3071" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg/220px-Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg/330px-Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg/440px-Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge%2C_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bonaparte_ante_la_Esfinge,_por_Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte_Before_the_Sphinx" title="Bonaparte Before the Sphinx">Bonaparte Before the Sphinx</a></i> (c. 1886) by <a href="/wiki/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me" title="Jean-Léon Gérôme">Jean-Léon Gérôme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hearst_Castle" title="Hearst Castle">Hearst Castle</a></div></div></div>
<p>After two months of planning, Bonaparte decided that France's naval strength was not yet sufficient to confront the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British Royal Navy.</a> He decided on a military expedition to seize <a href="/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet" title="Egypt Eyalet">Egypt</a> and thereby undermine Britain's access to its <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India#Trade" title="Company rule in India">trade interests in India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxviii_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-52">[45]</a></sup> Bonaparte wished to establish a French presence in the Middle East and join forces with <a href="/wiki/Tipu_Sultan" title="Tipu Sultan">Tipu Sultan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">Sultan of Mysore</a> who was an enemy of the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-83">[76]</a></sup> Napoleon assured the Directory that "as soon as he had conquered Egypt, he will establish relations with the Indian princes and, together with them, attack the English in their possessions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amini_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amini-84">[77]</a></sup> The Directory agreed in order to secure a trade route to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 1798, Bonaparte was elected a member of the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a>. His Egyptian expedition included a group of 167 scientists, with mathematicians, naturalists, chemists, and <a href="/wiki/Geodesy" title="Geodesy">geodesists</a> among them. Their discoveries included the <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_Stone" title="Rosetta Stone">Rosetta Stone</a>, and their work was published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Description_de_l%27%C3%89gypte" title="Description de l'Égypte">Description de l'Égypte</a></i> in 1809.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg"><img alt="Cavalry battlescene with pyramids in background" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1298" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/260px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/390px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/520px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Battle of the Pyramids</i> on 21 July 1798 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois,_Baron_Lejeune" title="Louis-François, Baron Lejeune">Louis-François, Baron Lejeune</a>, 1808</div></div></div>
<p>En route to Egypt, Bonaparte reached <a href="/wiki/Hospitaller_Malta" title="Hospitaller Malta">Malta</a> on 9 June 1798, then controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights Hospitaller</a>. Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_von_Hompesch_zu_Bolheim" title="Ferdinand von Hompesch zu Bolheim">Ferdinand von Hompesch zu Bolheim</a> surrendered after token resistance, and Bonaparte captured an important naval base with the loss of only three men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonaparte and his expedition eluded pursuit by the Royal Navy and landed at <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> on 1 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxviii_52-4"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-52">[45]</a></sup> He fought the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shubra_Khit" title="Battle of Shubra Khit">Battle of Shubra Khit</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a>, Egypt's ruling military caste. This helped the French practise their defensive tactic for the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Pyramids" title="Battle of the Pyramids">Battle of the Pyramids</a>, fought on 21 July, about 24 km (15 mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_pyramids" title="Egyptian pyramids">pyramids</a>. General Bonaparte's forces of 25,000 roughly equalled those of the Mamluks' Egyptian cavalry. Twenty-nine French<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[81]</a></sup> and approximately 2,000 Egyptians were killed. The victory boosted the morale of the French army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 August 1798, the British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Sir Horatio Nelson</a> captured or destroyed all but two vessels of the French fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Nile" title="Battle of the Nile">Battle of the Nile</a>, defeating Bonaparte's goal to strengthen the French position in the Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxx_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-90">[83]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITESHORT" title="Wikipedia:CITESHORT"><span title="More information is required to link this short citation to its long citation. (August 2021)">incomplete short citation</span></a></i>]</sup> His army had succeeded in a temporary increase of French power in Egypt, though it faced repeated uprisings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[84]</a></sup> In early 1799, he moved an army into the <a href="/wiki/Wilayah" title="Wilayah">Ottoman province</a> of Damascus (Syria and <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a>). Bonaparte led these 13,000 French soldiers in the conquest of the coastal towns of <a href="/wiki/Arish" title="Arish">Arish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">Jaffa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[85]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jaffa" title="Siege of Jaffa">attack on Jaffa</a> was particularly brutal. Bonaparte discovered that many of the defenders were former prisoners of war, ostensibly on <a href="/wiki/Parole" title="Parole">parole</a>, so he ordered the garrison and 1,400 prisoners to be executed by bayonet or drowning to save bullets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxx_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-90">[83]</a></sup> Men, women, and children were robbed and murdered for three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonaparte began with an army of 13,000 men; 1,500 were reported missing, 1,200 died in combat, and thousands perished from disease—mostly <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a>. He failed to <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Acre_(1799)" title="Siege of Acre (1799)">reduce the fortress</a> of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, so he marched his army back to Egypt in May. To speed up the retreat, Bonaparte ordered plague-stricken men to be poisoned with opium; the number who died remains disputed, ranging from a low of 30 to a high of 580. He also brought out 1,000 wounded men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[87]</a></sup> Back in Egypt on 25 July, Bonaparte defeated an <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Abukir_(1799)" title="Battle of Abukir (1799)">Ottoman amphibious invasion at Abukir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruler_of_France">Ruler of France</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">18 Brumaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_era" title="Napoleonic era">Napoleonic era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg"><img alt="Bonaparte in a simple general uniform in the middle of a scrum of red-robbed members of the Council of Five Hundred" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1953" data-file-width="1833" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/220px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/330px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/440px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General Bonaparte surrounded by members of the Council of Five Hundred during the Coup of 18 Brumaire, by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Bouchot" title="François Bouchot">François Bouchot</a></div></div></div>
<p>While in Egypt, Bonaparte stayed informed of European affairs. He learned that France had suffered a <a href="/wiki/Campaigns_of_1799_in_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Campaigns of 1799 in the French Revolutionary Wars">series of defeats</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Second_Coalition" title="War of the Second Coalition">War of the Second Coalition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-96">[89]</a></sup> On 24 August 1799, he took advantage of the temporary departure of British ships from French coastal ports and set sail for France, despite the fact that he had received no explicit orders from Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxx_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-90">[83]</a></sup> The army was left in the charge of <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Kl%C3%A9ber" title="Jean-Baptiste Kléber">Jean-Baptiste Kléber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unknown to Bonaparte, the Directory had sent him orders to return to ward off possible invasions of French soil, but poor lines of communication prevented the delivery of these messages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-96">[89]</a></sup> By the time that he reached Paris in October, France's situation had been improved by a series of victories. The Republic, however, was bankrupt and the ineffective Directory was unpopular with the French population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[91]</a></sup> The Directory discussed Bonaparte's "desertion" but was too weak to punish him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-96">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the failures in Egypt, Napoleon returned to a hero's welcome. He drew together an alliance with director <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Joseph_Siey%C3%A8s" title="Emmanuel Joseph Sieyès">Emmanuel Joseph Sieyès</a>, his brother Lucien, speaker of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Five_Hundred" title="Council of Five Hundred">Council of Five Hundred</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ducos" title="Roger Ducos">Roger Ducos</a>, director <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fouch%C3%A9" title="Joseph Fouché">Joseph Fouché</a>, and Talleyrand, and they overthrew the Directory by a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> on 9 November 1799 ("the 18th Brumaire" according to the revolutionary calendar), closing down the Council of Five Hundred. Napoleon became "first consul" for ten years, with two consuls appointed by him who had consultative voices only. His power was confirmed by the new "<a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Year_VIII" title="Constitution of the Year VIII">Constitution of the Year VIII</a>", originally devised by Sieyès to give Napoleon a minor role, but rewritten by Napoleon, and accepted by direct popular vote (3,000,000 in favour, 1,567 opposed). The constitution preserved the appearance of a republic but, in reality, established a dictatorship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Consulate">French Consulate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Consulate" title="French Consulate">French Consulate</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Second_Coalition" title="War of the Second Coalition">War of the Second Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres,_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4202" data-file-width="2665" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/170px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/255px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/340px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres,_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte,_First_Consul" title="Bonaparte, First Consul">Bonaparte, First Consul</a></i>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres" title="Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres">Ingres</a>. Posing <a href="/wiki/Hand-in-waistcoat" title="Hand-in-waistcoat">the hand inside the waistcoat</a> was often used in portraits of rulers to indicate calm and stable leadership.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="2244" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png/220px-5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png/330px-5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png/440px-5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:5f_Bonabarte_Premier_consul_-_AN_XI_1802.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Silver coin: 5 francs_AN XI, 1802, <b><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte,_First_Consul" title="Bonaparte, First Consul">Bonaparte, First Consul</a></b></div></div></div>
<p>Napoleon established a political system that historian <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Lyons" title="Martyn Lyons">Martyn Lyons</a> called "dictatorship by plebiscite".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111-101">[94]</a></sup> Worried by the democratic forces unleashed by the Revolution, but unwilling to ignore them entirely, Napoleon resorted to regular electoral consultations with the French people on his road to imperial power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111-101">[94]</a></sup> He drafted the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Year_VIII" title="Constitution of the Year VIII">Constitution of the Year VIII</a> and secured his own election as <a href="/wiki/French_Consulate" title="French Consulate">First Consul</a>, taking up residence at the Tuileries. The constitution was approved in <a href="/wiki/1800_French_constitutional_referendum" title="1800 French constitutional referendum">a rigged plebiscite</a> held the following January, with 99.94 percent officially listed as voting "yes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon's brother, Lucien, had falsified the returns to show that 3 million people had participated in the plebiscite. The real number was 1.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111-101">[94]</a></sup> Political observers at the time assumed the eligible French voting public numbered about 5 million people, so the regime artificially doubled the participation rate to indicate popular enthusiasm for the consulate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._111-101">[94]</a></sup> In the first few months of the consulate, with war in Europe still raging and internal instability still plaguing the country, Napoleon's grip on power remained very tenuous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the spring of 1800, Napoleon and his troops crossed the Swiss Alps into Italy, aiming to surprise the Austrian armies that had reoccupied the peninsula when Napoleon was still in Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[h]</a></sup> After a difficult crossing over the Alps, the French army entered the plains of Northern Italy virtually unopposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[98]</a></sup> While one French army approached from the north, the Austrians were busy with another stationed in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, which was <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Genoa_(1800)" title="Siege of Genoa (1800)">besieged</a> by a substantial force. The fierce resistance of this French army, under <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Mass%C3%A9na" title="André Masséna">André Masséna</a>, gave the northern force some time to carry out their operations with little interference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998,_p.235_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998,_p.235-107">[99]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_(circle)_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2375" data-file-width="3791" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg/220px-Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg/330px-Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg/440px-Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_%28circle%29_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jean-Simon_Berthelemy_(circle)_Napoleon_in_the_Battle_of_Maringo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marengo" title="Battle of Marengo">Battle of Marengo</a> was Napoleon's first great victory as head of state.</div></div></div>
<p>After spending several days looking for each other, the two armies collided at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marengo" title="Battle of Marengo">Battle of Marengo</a> on 14 June. <a href="/wiki/Michael_von_Melas" title="Michael von Melas">General Melas</a> had a numerical advantage, fielding about 30,000 Austrian soldiers while Napoleon commanded 24,000 French troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[100]</a></sup> The battle began favourably for the Austrians as their initial attack surprised the French and gradually drove them back. Melas stated that he had won the battle and retired to his headquarters around 3 pm, leaving his subordinates in charge of pursuing the French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[101]</a></sup> The French lines never broke during their tactical retreat. Napoleon constantly rode out among the troops urging them to stand and fight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296-110">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>Late in the afternoon, a full division under <a href="/wiki/Louis_Desaix" title="Louis Desaix">Desaix</a> arrived on the field and reversed the tide of the battle. A series of artillery barrages and cavalry charges decimated the Austrian army, which fled over the <a href="/wiki/Bormida_(river)" title="Bormida (river)">Bormida River</a> back to <a href="/wiki/Alessandria" title="Alessandria">Alessandria</a>, leaving behind 14,000 casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296-110">[102]</a></sup> The following day, the Austrian army agreed to abandon Northern Italy once more with the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Alessandria" title="Convention of Alessandria">Convention of Alessandria</a>, which granted them safe passage to friendly soil in exchange for their fortresses throughout the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler,_David_1966,_p._296-110">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although critics have blamed Napoleon for several tactical mistakes preceding the battle, they have also praised his audacity for selecting a risky campaign strategy, choosing to invade the Italian peninsula from the north when the vast majority of French invasions came from the west, near or along the coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler,_David_1966,_pp._298-304_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler,_David_1966,_pp._298-304-111">[103]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/David_G._Chandler" title="David G. Chandler">David G. Chandler</a> points out, Napoleon spent almost a year getting the Austrians out of Italy in his first campaign. In 1800, it took him only a month to achieve the same goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler,_David_1966,_pp._298-304_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler,_David_1966,_pp._298-304-111">[103]</a></sup> German strategist and field marshal <a href="/wiki/Alfred_von_Schlieffen" title="Alfred von Schlieffen">Alfred von Schlieffen</a> concluded that "Bonaparte did not annihilate his enemy but eliminated him and rendered him harmless" while "[attaining] the object of the campaign: the conquest of North Italy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon's triumph at Marengo secured his political authority and boosted his popularity back home, but it did not lead to an immediate peace. Bonaparte's brother, Joseph, led the complex negotiations in <a href="/wiki/Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Lunéville">Lunéville</a> and reported that Austria, emboldened by British support, would not acknowledge the new territory that France had acquired. As negotiations became increasingly fractious, Bonaparte gave orders to his general <a href="/wiki/Jean_Victor_Marie_Moreau" title="Jean Victor Marie Moreau">Moreau</a> to strike Austria once more. Moreau and the French swept through <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and scored an overwhelming victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenlinden" title="Battle of Hohenlinden">Hohenlinden</a> in December 1800. As a result, the Austrians capitulated and signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Treaty of Lunéville</a> in February 1801. The treaty reaffirmed and expanded earlier French gains at <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Campo Formio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schom_1997,_p.302_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schom_1997,_p.302-113">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temporary_peace_in_Europe">Temporary peace in Europe</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a></div>
<p>After a decade of constant warfare, France and Britain signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">Treaty of Amiens</a> in March 1802, bringing the Revolutionary Wars to an end.
