Amiens called for the withdrawal of British troops from recently conquered colonial territories as well as for assurances to curtail the expansionary goals of the French Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998,_p.235_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998,_p.235-107">[99]</a></sup> With Europe at peace and the economy recovering, Napoleon's popularity soared to its highest levels under the consulate, both domestically and abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_pp._111-4_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_pp._111-4-114">[106]</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/1802_French_constitutional_referendum" title="1802 French constitutional referendum">new plebiscite</a> during the spring of 1802, the French public came out in huge numbers to approve a constitution that made the Consulate permanent, essentially elevating Napoleon to dictator for life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_pp._111-4_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_pp._111-4-114">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>Whereas the plebiscite two years earlier had brought out 1.5 million people to the polls, the new referendum enticed 3.6 million to go and vote (72 percent of all eligible voters).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113-115">[107]</a></sup> There was no secret ballot in 1802 and few people wanted to openly defy the regime. The constitution gained approval with over 99% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113-115">[107]</a></sup> His broad powers were spelled out in the new constitution: <i>Article 1. The French people name, and the Senate proclaims Napoleon-Bonaparte First Consul for Life.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[108]</a></sup> After 1802, he was generally referred to as Napoleon rather than Bonaparte.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m290_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-m290-45">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisiana_Purchase.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2414" data-file-width="3433" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Louisiana_Purchase.png/220px-Louisiana_Purchase.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Louisiana_Purchase.png/330px-Louisiana_Purchase.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Louisiana_Purchase.png/440px-Louisiana_Purchase.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louisiana_Purchase.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1803 <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> totalled 2,144,480 square kilometres (827,987 square miles), doubling the size of the United States.</div></div></div>
<p>The brief peace in Europe allowed Napoleon to focus on <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonies</a> abroad. <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> had managed to acquire a high level of political autonomy during the Revolutionary Wars, with <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint L'Ouverture</a> installing himself as de facto dictator by 1801. Napoleon saw a chance to reestablish control over the colony when he signed the Treaty of Amiens. In the 18th century, Saint-Domingue had been France's most profitable colony, producing more sugar than all the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> colonies combined. However, during the Revolution, the National Convention voted to abolish slavery in February 1794.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[109]</a></sup> Aware of the expenses required to fund his wars in Europe, Napoleon made the decision to <a href="/wiki/Law_of_20_May_1802" title="Law of 20 May 1802">reinstate slavery</a> in all French Caribbean colonies. The 1794 decree had only affected the colonies of Saint-Domingue, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">Guiana</a>, and did not take effect in <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Reunion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, the last of which had been captured by the British and as such remained unaffected by French law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> slavery had been abolished (and its ban violently enforced) by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugues" title="Victor Hugues">Victor Hugues</a> against opposition from slaveholders thanks to the 1794 law. However, when slavery was reinstated in 1802, a <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave revolt</a> broke out under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Louis_Delgr%C3%A8s" title="Louis Delgrès">Louis Delgrès</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[111]</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Law_of_20_May_1802" title="Law of 20 May 1802">Law of 20 May</a> had the express purpose of reinstating slavery in Saint-Domingue, Guadeloupe and French Guiana, and restored slavery throughout most of the French colonial empire (excluding Saint-Domingue) for another half a century, while the French <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">transatlantic slave trade</a> continued for another twenty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2014301_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2014301-120">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clrjames_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-clrjames-121">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon sent <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue_expedition" title="Saint-Domingue expedition">an expedition</a> under his brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc_(general,_born_1772)" title="Charles Leclerc (general, born 1772)">General Leclerc</a> to reassert control over Saint-Domingue. Although the French managed to capture Toussaint Louverture, the expedition failed when high rates of disease crippled the French army, and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a> won a string of victories, first against Leclerc, and when he died from yellow fever, then against <a href="/wiki/Donatien-Marie-Joseph_de_Vimeur,_vicomte_de_Rochambeau" title="Donatien-Marie-Joseph de Vimeur, vicomte de Rochambeau">Donatien-Marie-Joseph de Vimeur, vicomte de Rochambeau</a>, whom Napoleon sent to relieve Leclerc with another 20,000 men. In May 1803, Napoleon acknowledged defeat, and the last 8,000 French troops left the island and the slaves proclaimed an independent republic that they called <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> in 1804. In the process, Dessalines became arguably the most successful military commander in the struggle against Napoleonic France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2014303_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2014303-126">[118]</a></sup> Seeing the failure of his efforts in Haiti, Napoleon decided in 1803 to <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">sell</a> the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Territory" title="Louisiana Territory">Louisiana Territory</a> to the United States, instantly doubling the size of the U.S. The selling price in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> was less than three cents per acre, a total of $15 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts,_Andrew_2014_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts,_Andrew_2014-4">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>The peace with Britain proved to be uneasy and controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[120]</a></sup> Britain did not evacuate Malta as promised and protested against Bonaparte's <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> of Piedmont and his <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Mediation" title="Act of Mediation">Act of Mediation</a>, which established a new <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_in_the_Napoleonic_era" title="Switzerland in the Napoleonic era">Swiss Confederation</a>. Neither of these territories were covered by Amiens, but they inflamed tensions significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[121]</a></sup> The dispute culminated in a declaration of war by Britain in May 1803; Napoleon responded by reassembling the invasion camp at Boulogne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rxx_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-90">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Empire">French Empire</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronation_of_Napoleon_I" title="Coronation of Napoleon I">Coronation of Napoleon I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_(1805-1807).jpg"><img alt="Colored painting depicting Napoleon crowning his wife inside of a cathedral" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3773" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg/220px-Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg/330px-Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg/440px-Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_%281805-1807%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacques-Louis_David_-_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_(1805-1807).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Coronation_of_Napoleon" title="The Coronation of Napoleon">The Coronation of Napoleon</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Louis_David" title="Jacques-Louis David">Jacques-Louis David</a> (1804)</div></div></div>
<p>During the consulate, Napoleon faced several royalist and Jacobin <a href="/wiki/Assassination_attempts_on_Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Assassination attempts on Napoleon Bonaparte">assassination plots</a>, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Conspiration_des_poignards" title="Conspiration des poignards">Conspiration des poignards</a></i> (Dagger plot) in October 1800 and the <a href="/wiki/Plot_of_the_rue_Saint-Nicaise" title="Plot of the rue Saint-Nicaise">Plot of the Rue Saint-Nicaise</a> (also known as the <i>Infernal Machine</i>) two months later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[122]</a></sup> In January 1804, his police uncovered an assassination plot against him that involved Moreau and which was ostensibly sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> family, the former rulers of France. On the advice of Talleyrand, Napoleon ordered the kidnapping of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine,_Duke_of_Enghien" title="Louis Antoine, Duke of Enghien">Duke of Enghien</a>, violating the sovereignty of <a href="/wiki/Baden" title="Baden">Baden</a>. The Duke was quickly executed after a secret military trial, even though he had not been involved in the plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[123]</a></sup> Enghien's execution infuriated royal courts throughout Europe, becoming one of the contributing political factors for the outbreak of the Napoleonic Wars.
</p><p>To expand his power, Napoleon used these <a href="/wiki/Assassination_attempts_on_Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Assassination attempts on Napoleon Bonaparte">assassination plots</a> to justify the creation of an imperial system based on the <a href="/wiki/Roman_imperial_cult" title="Roman imperial cult">Roman model.</a>He believed that a Bourbon restoration would be more difficult if his family's succession was entrenched in the constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m297_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-m297-132">[124]</a></sup> Launching yet <a href="/wiki/1804_French_constitutional_referendum" title="1804 French constitutional referendum">another referendum</a>, Napoleon was elected as <i>Emperor of the French</i> by a tally exceeding 99%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113-115">[107]</a></sup> As with the Life Consulate two years earlier, this referendum produced heavy participation, bringing out almost 3.6 million voters to the polls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113_115-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons,_Martyn_1994,_p._113-115">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>A keen observer of Bonaparte's rise to absolute power, <a href="/wiki/Madame_de_R%C3%A9musat" title="Madame de Rémusat">Madame de Rémusat</a>, explains that "men worn out by the turmoil of the Revolution […] looked for the domination of an able ruler" and that "people believed quite sincerely that Bonaparte, whether as consul or emperor, would exert his authority and save [them] from the perils of anarchy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[125]</a></sup>"
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_(Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg/220px-La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg/330px-La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg/440px-La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_%28Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_salle_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_(Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Fontainebleau).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon's throne room at Fontainebleau</div></div></div>
<p>Napoleon's coronation, at which <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_VII" title="Pope Pius VII">Pope Pius VII</a> officiated, took place at <a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre-Dame de Paris">Notre Dame de Paris</a>, on 2 December 1804. Two separate crowns were brought for the ceremony: a golden laurel wreath recalling the Roman Empire and a replica of Charlemagne's crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-134">[126]</a></sup> Napoleon entered the ceremony wearing the laurel wreath and kept it on his head throughout the proceedings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-134">[126]</a></sup> For the official coronation, he raised the Charlemagne crown over his own head in a symbolic gesture, but never placed it on top because he was already wearing the golden wreath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-134">[126]</a></sup> Instead he placed the crown on <a href="/wiki/Empress_Jos%C3%A9phine" title="Empress Joséphine">Josephine's</a> head, the event commemorated in the officially sanctioned painting by <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Louis_David" title="Jacques-Louis David">Jacques-Louis David</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_134-3"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-134">[126]</a></sup> Napoleon was also crowned <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_Crown_of_Lombardy" title="Iron Crown of Lombardy">Iron Crown of Lombardy</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Milan_Cathedral" title="Milan Cathedral">Cathedral of Milan</a> on 26 May 1805. He created eighteen <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marshals_of_France" title="List of Marshals of France">Marshals of the Empire</a> from among his top generals to secure the allegiance of the army on 18 May 1804, the official start of the Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Third_Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulm_capitulation.jpg"><img alt="Colored painting depicting Napoleon receiving the surrender of the Austrian generals, with the opposing armies and the city of Ulm in the background" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1246" data-file-width="1973" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/220px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/330px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/440px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulm_capitulation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon and the <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Armée">Grande Armée</a></i> receive the surrender of <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Karl_Mack_von_Leiberich" title="Karl Mack von Leiberich">General Mack</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ulm" title="Battle of Ulm">Battle of Ulm</a> in October 1805. The decisive finale of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Campaign</a> raised the tally of captured Austrian soldiers to 60,000. With the Austrian army destroyed, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> would fall to the French in November.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a> had broken the Peace of Amiens by declaring war on France in May 1803.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[128]</a></sup> In December 1804, an Anglo-Swedish agreement became the first step towards the creation of the Third Coalition. By April 1805, Britain had also signed an alliance with Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[129]</a></sup> Austria had been defeated by France twice in recent memory and wanted revenge, so it joined the coalition a few months later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the formation of the Third Coalition, Napoleon had assembled an invasion force, the <i>Armée d'Angleterre</i>, around six camps at <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne</a> in Northern France. He intended to use this invasion force to strike at England. They never invaded, but Napoleon's troops received careful and invaluable training for future military operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[131]</a></sup> The men at Boulogne formed the core for what Napoleon later called <i>La Grande Armée</i>. At the start, this French army had about 200,000 men organized into seven <a href="/wiki/Corps" title="Corps">corps</a>, which were large field units that contained 36–40 <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannons</a> each and were capable of independent action until other corps could come to the rescue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>A single corps properly situated in a strong defensive position could survive at least a day without support, giving the <i>Grande Armée</i> countless strategic and tactical options on every campaign. On top of these forces, Napoleon created a <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> reserve of 22,000 organized into two <a href="/wiki/Cuirassier" title="Cuirassier">cuirassier</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a>, four mounted <a href="/wiki/Dragoon" title="Dragoon">dragoon</a> divisions, one division of dismounted dragoons, and one of light cavalry, all supported by 24 <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> pieces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_p._333_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_p._333-141">[133]</a></sup> By 1805, the <i>Grande Armée</i> had grown to a force of 350,000 men,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_p._333_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_p._333-141">[133]</a></sup> who were well equipped, well trained, and led by competent officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon knew that the French fleet could not defeat the Royal Navy in a head-to-head battle, so he planned to lure it away from the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> through diversionary tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998,_p.321_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998,_p.321-143">[135]</a></sup> The main strategic idea involved the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> escaping from the British blockades of <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> and threatening to attack the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>. In the face of this attack, it was hoped, the British would weaken their defence of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Approaches" title="Western Approaches">Western Approaches</a> by sending ships to the Caribbean, allowing a combined Franco-Spanish fleet to take control of the English channel long enough for French armies to cross and <a href="/wiki/Napoleon%27s_planned_invasion_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Napoleon's planned invasion of the United Kingdom">invade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998,_p.321_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998,_p.321-143">[135]</a></sup> However, the plan unravelled after the British victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Finisterre_(1805)" title="Battle of Cape Finisterre (1805)">Battle of Cape Finisterre</a> in July 1805. French <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Charles_Villeneuve" title="Pierre-Charles Villeneuve">Admiral Villeneuve</a> then retreated to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> instead of linking up with French naval forces at Brest for an attack on the English Channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2792" data-file-width="1812" decoding="async" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/220px-Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/330px-Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/440px-Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_in_Coronation_Robes_by_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoléon in his coronation robes by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard" title="François Gérard">François Gérard</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1805</span></div></div></div>
<p>By August 1805, Napoleon had realized that the strategic situation had changed fundamentally. Facing a potential invasion from his continental enemies, he decided to strike first and turned his army's sights from the English Channel to the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>. His basic objective was to destroy the isolated Austrian armies in Southern Germany before their Russian allies could arrive. On 25 September, after great secrecy and feverish marching, 200,000 French troops began to cross the Rhine on a front of 260 km (160 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>Austrian commander <a href="/wiki/Karl_Mack_von_Leiberich" title="Karl Mack von Leiberich">Karl Mack</a> had gathered the greater part of the Austrian army at the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>. Napoleon swung his forces to the southeast and the <i>Grande Armée</i> performed an elaborate wheeling movement that outflanked the Austrian positions. The <a href="/wiki/Ulm_campaign" title="Ulm campaign">Ulm Maneuver</a> completely surprised General Mack, who belatedly understood that his army had been cut off. After some minor engagements that culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ulm" title="Battle of Ulm">Battle of Ulm</a>, Mack finally surrendered after realizing that there was no way to break out of the French encirclement. For just 2,000 French casualties, Napoleon had managed to capture a total of 60,000 Austrian soldiers through his army's rapid marching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[139]</a></sup> Napoleon wrote after the conflict:
</p>
<blockquote><p>"I have accomplished my object, I have destroyed the Austrian army by simply marching."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[140]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ulm_campaign" title="Ulm campaign">Ulm Campaign</a> is generally regarded as a strategic masterpiece and was influential in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Schlieffen_Plan" title="Schlieffen Plan">Schlieffen Plan</a> in the late 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[141]</a></sup> For the French, this spectacular victory on land was soured by the decisive victory that the Royal Navy attained at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> on 21 October. After Trafalgar, the Royal Navy was never again seriously challenged by a French fleet in a large-scale engagement for the duration of the Napoleonic Wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlover1967233–252_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlover1967233–252-150">[142]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITESHORT" title="Wikipedia:CITESHORT"><span title="More information is required to link this short citation to its long citation. (August 2021)">incomplete short citation</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_(Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1983" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg/300px-La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg/450px-La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg/600px-La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_%28Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_bataille_d%27Austerlitz._2_decembre_1805_(Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon at the Battle of Austerlitz, by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard" title="François Gérard">François Gérard</a> 1805. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, also known as the Battle of the Three Emperors, was one of Napoleon's many victories, where the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French Empire</a> defeated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Coalition" title="Third Coalition">Third Coalition</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Following the Ulm Campaign, French forces managed to capture <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in November. The fall of Vienna provided the French a huge bounty as they captured 100,000 muskets, 500 cannons, and the intact bridges across the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973407_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973407-151">[143]</a></sup> At this critical juncture, both <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Tsar Alexander I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis II, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor Francis II</a> decided to engage Napoleon in battle, despite reservations from some of their subordinates. Napoleon sent his army north in pursuit of the Allies but then ordered his forces to retreat so that he could feign a grave weakness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-152">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Desperate to lure the Allies into battle, Napoleon gave every indication in the days preceding the engagement that the French army was in a pitiful state, even abandoning the dominant Pratzen Heights, a sloping hill near the village of <a href="/wiki/Austerlitz,_Netherlands" title="Austerlitz, Netherlands">Austerlitz</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> on 2 December, he deployed the French army below the Pratzen Heights and deliberately weakened his right flank, enticing the Allies to launch a major assault there in the hopes of rolling up the whole French line. A forced march from Vienna by <a href="/wiki/Louis-Nicolas_Davout" title="Louis-Nicolas Davout">Marshal Davout</a> and his <a href="/wiki/III_Corps_(Grande_Arm%C3%A9e)" title="III Corps (Grande Armée)">III Corps</a> plugged the gap left by Napoleon just in time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-152">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, the heavy Allied deployment against the French right flank weakened their center on the Pratzen Heights, which was viciously attacked by the <a href="/wiki/IV_Corps_(Grande_Arm%C3%A9e)" title="IV Corps (Grande Armée)">IV Corps</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jean-de-Dieu_Soult" title="Jean-de-Dieu Soult">Marshal Soult</a>. With the Allied center demolished, the French swept through both enemy flanks and sent the Allies fleeing chaotically, capturing thousands of prisoners in the process. The battle is often seen as a tactical masterpiece because of the near-perfect execution of a calibrated but dangerous plan—of the same stature as <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">Cannae</a>, the celebrated triumph by <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a> some 2,000 years before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-152">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Allied disaster at Austerlitz significantly shook the faith of Emperor Francis in the British-led war effort. France and Austria agreed to an armistice immediately and the Treaty of Pressburg followed shortly after on 26 December. Pressburg took Austria out of both the war and the Coalition while reinforcing the earlier treaties of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Campo Formio</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Lunéville</a> between the two powers. The treaty confirmed the Austrian loss of lands to France in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Napoleonic)" title="Kingdom of Italy (Napoleonic)">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Bavaria" title="Electorate of Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, and lands in Germany to Napoleon's German allies. It also imposed an indemnity of 40 million francs on the defeated Habsburgs and allowed the fleeing Russian troops free passage through hostile territories and back to their home soil. Napoleon went on to say, "The battle of Austerlitz is the finest of all I have fought".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[145]</a></sup> Frank McLynn suggests that Napoleon was so successful at Austerlitz that he lost touch with reality, and what used to be French foreign policy became a "personal Napoleonic one".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Cronin" title="Vincent Cronin">Vincent Cronin</a> disagrees, stating that Napoleon was not overly ambitious for himself, "he embodied the ambitions of thirty million Frenchmen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle-Eastern_alliances">Middle-Eastern alliances</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ottoman_alliance" title="Franco-Ottoman alliance">Franco-Ottoman alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franco-Persian_alliance" title="Franco-Persian alliance">Franco-Persian alliance</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="1127" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/220px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/330px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/440px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Iranian envoy Mirza Mohammed Reza-Qazvini meeting with Napoleon I at the <a href="/wiki/Finckenstein_Palace" title="Finckenstein Palace">Finckenstein Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Prussia" title="West Prussia">West Prussia</a>, 27 April 1807, to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Finckenstein" title="Treaty of Finckenstein">Treaty of Finckenstein</a></div></div></div>
<p>Napoleon continued to entertain a grand scheme to establish a French presence in the Middle East in order to put pressure on <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and Russia, and perhaps form an alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-83">[76]</a></sup> In February 1806, Ottoman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> recognised Napoleon as <i>Emperor</i>. He also opted for an alliance with France, calling France "our sincere and natural ally".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[148]</a></sup> That decision brought the Ottoman Empire into a losing war against Russia and Britain. A Franco-Persian alliance was also formed between Napoleon and the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persian Empire</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fath-Ali_Shah_Qajar" title="Fath-Ali Shah Qajar">Fat′h-Ali Shah Qajar</a>. It collapsed in 1807 when France and Russia themselves formed an unexpected alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-83">[76]</a></sup> In the end, Napoleon had made no effective alliances in the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESicker200199_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESicker200199-157">[149]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition_and_Tilsit">War of the Fourth Coalition and Tilsit</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition" title="War of the Fourth Coalition">War of the Fourth Coalition</a></div>
<p>After Austerlitz, Napoleon established the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a> in 1806. A collection of German states intended to serve as a buffer zone between France and Central Europe, the creation of the Confederation spelled the end of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and significantly alarmed the Prussians. The brazen reorganization of German territory by the French risked threatening Prussian influence in the region, if not eliminating it outright. War fever in Berlin rose steadily throughout the summer of 1806. At the insistence of his court, especially his wife <a href="/wiki/Louise_of_Mecklenburg-Strelitz" title="Louise of Mecklenburg-Strelitz">Queen Louise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_III_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William III of Prussia">Frederick William III</a> decided to challenge the French domination of Central Europe by going to war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iena.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1655" data-file-width="1955" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/220px-Iena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/330px-Iena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/440px-Iena.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iena.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon reviewing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Imperial_Guard" title="French Imperial Guard">Imperial Guard</a> before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena" title="Battle of Jena">Battle of Jena</a></div></div></div>
<p>The initial military manoeuvres began in September 1806. In a letter to <a href="/wiki/Jean-de-Dieu_Soult" title="Jean-de-Dieu Soult">Marshal Soult</a> detailing the plan for the campaign, Napoleon described the essential features of Napoleonic warfare and introduced the phrase <i>le bataillon-carré</i> ("square battalion").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8-159">[151]</a></sup> In the <i>bataillon-carré</i> system, the various corps of the <i>Grande Armée</i> would march uniformly together in close supporting distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8-159">[151]</a></sup> If any single corps was attacked, the others could quickly spring into action and arrive to help.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-160">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon invaded Prussia with 180,000 troops, rapidly marching on the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Saale" title="Saale">River Saale</a>. As in previous campaigns, his fundamental objective was to destroy one opponent before reinforcements from another could tip the balance of the war. Upon learning the whereabouts of the Prussian army, the French swung westwards and crossed the Saale with overwhelming force. At the twin <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena%E2%80%93Auerstedt" title="Battle of Jena–Auerstedt">battles of Jena and Auerstedt</a>, fought on 14 October, the French convincingly defeated the Prussians and inflicted heavy casualties. With several major commanders dead or incapacitated, the Prussian king proved incapable of effectively commanding the army, which began to quickly disintegrate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-160">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a vaunted pursuit that epitomized the "peak of Napoleonic warfare", according to historian Richard Brooks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-160">[152]</a></sup> the French managed to capture 140,000 soldiers, over 2,000 cannons and hundreds of ammunition wagons, all in a single month. Historian David Chandler wrote of the Prussian forces: "Never has the morale of any army been more completely shattered".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966,_p._467-8-159">[151]</a></sup> Despite their overwhelming defeat, the Prussians refused to negotiate with the French until the Russians had an opportunity to enter the fight.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tilsitz_1807.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1504" data-file-width="1933" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/220px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/330px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/440px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tilsitz_1807.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a>: Napoleon meeting with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a> on a raft in the middle of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neman_River" title="Neman River">Neman River</a></div></div></div>
<p>Following his triumph, Napoleon imposed the first elements of the Continental System through the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Decree" title="Berlin Decree">Berlin Decree</a> issued in November 1806. The Continental System, which prohibited European nations from trading with Britain, was widely violated throughout his reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[154]</a></sup> In the next few months, Napoleon marched against the advancing Russian armies through Poland and was involved in the bloody stalemate at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Eylau" title="Battle of Eylau">Battle of Eylau</a> in February 1807.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[155]</a></sup> After a period of rest and consolidation on both sides, the war restarted in June with an initial struggle at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Heilsberg" title="Battle of Heilsberg">Heilsberg</a> that proved indecisive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-164">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 June Napoleon obtained an overwhelming victory over the Russians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Friedland" title="Battle of Friedland">Battle of Friedland</a>, wiping out the majority of the Russian army in a very bloody struggle. The scale of their defeat convinced the Russians to make peace with the French. On 19 June, Tsar Alexander sent an envoy to seek an armistice with Napoleon. The latter assured the envoy that the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula River</a> represented the natural borders between French and Russian influence in Europe. On that basis, the two emperors began peace negotiations at the town of <a href="/wiki/Sovetsk,_Kaliningrad_Oblast" title="Sovetsk, Kaliningrad Oblast">Tilsit</a> after meeting on an iconic raft on the <a href="/wiki/Neman" title="Neman">River Niemen</a>. The very first thing Alexander said to Napoleon was probably well-calibrated: "I hate the English as much as you do".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-164">[156]</a></sup> Their meeting lasted two hours. Despite waging wars against each other the two Emperors were very much impressed and fascinated by one another.  “Never,” said Alexander afterward, “did I love any man as I loved that man.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>Alexander faced pressure from his brother, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Konstantin_Pavlovich_of_Russia" title="Grand Duke Konstantin Pavlovich of Russia">Duke Constantine</a>, to make peace with Napoleon. Given the victory he had just achieved, the French emperor offered the Russians relatively lenient terms—demanding that Russia join the Continental System, withdraw its forces from <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, and hand over the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Islands" title="Ionian Islands">Ionian Islands</a> to France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts458459_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts458459-166">[158]</a></sup> By contrast, Napoleon dictated very harsh peace terms for Prussia, despite the ceaseless exhortations of <a href="/wiki/Louise_of_Mecklenburg-Strelitz" title="Louise of Mecklenburg-Strelitz">Queen Louise</a>. Wiping out half of Prussian territories from the map, Napoleon created a new kingdom of 2,800 square kilometres (1,100 sq mi) called <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Westphalia" title="Kingdom of Westphalia">Westphalia</a> and appointed his young brother Jérôme as its monarch. Prussia's humiliating treatment at Tilsit caused a deep and bitter antagonism that festered as the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_era" title="Napoleonic era">Napoleonic era</a> progressed. Moreover, Alexander's pretensions at friendship with Napoleon led the latter to seriously misjudge the true intentions of his Russian counterpart, who would violate numerous provisions of the treaty in the next few years. Despite these problems, the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a> at last gave Napoleon a respite from war and allowed him to return to France, which he had not seen in over 300 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts459461_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts459461-167">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peninsular_War_and_Erfurt">Peninsular War and Erfurt</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a></div>
<p>The settlements at Tilsit gave Napoleon time to organize his empire. One of his major objectives became enforcing the Continental System against the British forces. He decided to focus his attention on the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>, which consistently violated his trade prohibitions. After defeat in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Oranges" title="War of the Oranges">War of the Oranges</a> in 1801, Portugal adopted a double-sided policy.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3251" data-file-width="2114" decoding="async" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/220px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/330px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/440px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>, Napoleon's brother, as King of Spain</div></div></div>
<p>Unhappy with this change of policy by the Portuguese government, Napoleon negotiated a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(October_1807)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (October 1807)">secret treaty</a> with <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV of Spain</a> and sent an army to invade Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[160]</a></sup> On 17 October 1807, 24,000 French troops under <a href="/wiki/Jean-Andoche_Junot" title="Jean-Andoche Junot">General Junot</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> with <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> cooperation and headed towards Portugal to enforce Napoleon's orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[161]</a></sup> This attack was the first step in what would eventually become the Peninsular War, a six-year struggle that significantly sapped French strength. Throughout the winter of 1808, French agents became increasingly involved in Spanish internal affairs, attempting to incite discord between members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Spanish royal family</a>. On 16 February 1808, secret French machinations finally materialized when Napoleon announced that he would intervene to mediate between the rival political factions in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Marshal Murat</a> led 120,000 troops into Spain. The French arrived in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> on 24 March,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[163]</a></sup> where wild riots against the occupation erupted just a few weeks later. Napoleon appointed his brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>, as the new King of Spain in the summer of 1808. The appointment enraged a heavily religious and conservative Spanish population. Resistance to French aggression soon spread throughout Spain. The shocking French defeats at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bail%C3%A9n" title="Battle of Bailén">Battle of Bailén</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimiero" title="Battle of Vimiero">Battle of Vimiero</a> gave hope to Napoleon's enemies and partly persuaded the French emperor to intervene in person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler620_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler620-172">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before going to Iberia, Napoleon decided to address several lingering issues with the Russians. At the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> in October 1808, Napoleon hoped to keep Russia on his side during the upcoming struggle in Spain and during any potential conflict against Austria. The two sides reached an agreement, the Erfurt Convention, that called upon Britain to cease its war against France, that recognized the Russian conquest of <a href="/wiki/Sweden%E2%80%93Finland" title="Sweden–Finland">Finland</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gustavian_era" title="Gustavian era">Sweden</a> and made it an <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">autonomous Grand Duchy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[165]</a></sup> and that affirmed Russian support for France in a possible war against Austria "to the best of its ability".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon then returned to France and prepared for war. The <i>Grande Armée</i>, under the Emperor's personal command, rapidly crossed the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> River in November 1808 and inflicted a series of crushing defeats against the Spanish forces. After clearing the last Spanish force guarding the capital at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Somosierra" title="Battle of Somosierra">Somosierra</a>, Napoleon entered Madrid on 4 December with 80,000 troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[167]</a></sup> He then unleashed his soldiers against <a href="/wiki/John_Moore_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Moore (British Army officer)">Moore</a> and the British forces. The British were swiftly driven to the coast, and they withdrew from Spain entirely after a last stand at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Corunna" title="Battle of Corunna">Battle of Corunna</a> in January 1809 and the death of <a href="/wiki/John_Moore_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Moore (British Army officer)">Moore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid,_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="1782" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg/220px-Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg/330px-Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg/440px-Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid%2C_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Capitulation_de_Madrid,_le_4_d%C3%A9cembre_1808.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon accepting the surrender of <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, 4 December 1808</div></div></div>
<p>Napoleon would end up leaving Iberia in order to deal with the Austrians in Central Europe, but the Peninsular War continued on long after his absence. He never returned to Spain after the 1808 campaign. Several months after Corunna, the British sent another army to the peninsula under Arthur Wellesley, the future <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>. The war then settled into a complex and asymmetric strategic deadlock where all sides struggled to gain the upper hand. The highlight of the conflict became the brutal <i><a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a></i> that engulfed much of the Spanish countryside. Both sides committed the worst atrocities of the Napoleonic Wars during this phase of the conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-177">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>The vicious guerrilla fighting in Spain, largely absent from the French campaigns in Central Europe, severely disrupted the French lines of supply and communication. Although France maintained roughly 300,000 troops in Iberia during the Peninsular War, the vast majority were tied down to garrison duty and to intelligence operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-177">[169]</a></sup> The French were never able to concentrate all of their forces effectively, prolonging the war until events elsewhere in Europe finally turned the tide in favour of the Allies. After the invasion of Russia in 1812, the number of French troops in Spain vastly declined as Napoleon needed reinforcements to conserve his strategic position in Europe. By 1814, after scores of battles and sieges throughout Iberia, the Allies had managed to push the French out of the peninsula.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The impact of the Napoleonic invasion of Spain and ousting of the Spanish Bourbon monarchy in favour of his brother Joseph had an enormous impact on the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish empire</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Spanish America</a> many local elites formed juntas and set up mechanisms to rule in the name of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a>, whom they considered the legitimate Spanish monarch. The outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> in most of the empire was a result of Napoleon's destabilizing actions in Spain and led to the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongmen</a> in the wake of these wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[170]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition_and_Marie_Louise">War of the Fifth Coalition and Marie Louise</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition" title="War of the Fifth Coalition">War of the Fifth Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Wagram.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2326" data-file-width="3154" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/220px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/330px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/440px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Wagram.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a>, painted by <a href="/wiki/Horace_Vernet" title="Horace Vernet">Horace Vernet</a></div></div></div>
<p>After four years on the sidelines, Austria sought another war with France to avenge its recent defeats. Austria could not count on Russian support because the latter was at war with <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_War_(1807%E2%80%931812)" title="Anglo-Russian War (1807–1812)">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_War" title="Finnish War">Sweden</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1806%E2%80%931812)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1806–1812)">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1809. <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_III_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William III of Prussia">Frederick William</a> of Prussia initially promised to help the Austrians but reneged before conflict began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-179">[171]</a></sup> A report from the Austrian finance minister suggested that the treasury would run out of money by the middle of 1809 if the large army that the Austrians had formed since the Third Coalition remained mobilized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-179">[171]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Charles,_Duke_of_Teschen" title="Archduke Charles, Duke of Teschen">Archduke Charles</a> warned that the Austrians were not ready for another showdown with Napoleon, a stance that landed him in the so-called "peace party", he did not want to see the army demobilized either.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_179-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_&amp;_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-179">[171]</a></sup> On 8 February 1809, the advocates for war finally succeeded when the Imperial Government secretly decided on another confrontation against the French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gill4445_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gill4445-180">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early morning of 10 April, leading elements of the Austrian army crossed the <a href="/wiki/Inn_(river)" title="Inn (river)">Inn River</a> and invaded Bavaria. The early Austrian attack surprised the French; Napoleon himself was still in Paris when he heard about the invasion. He arrived at <a href="/wiki/Donauw%C3%B6rth" title="Donauwörth">Donauwörth</a> on the 17th to find the <i>Grande Armée</i> in a dangerous position, with its two wings separated by 120 km (75 mi) and joined by a thin cordon of Bavarian troops. Charles pressed the left wing of the French army and hurled his men towards the III Corps of Marshal Davout. In response, Napoleon came up with a plan to cut off the Austrians in the celebrated <i>Landshut Maneuver</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[173]</a></sup> He realigned the axis of his army and marched his soldiers towards the town of <a href="/wiki/Eckm%C3%BChl" title="Eckmühl">Eckmühl</a>. The French scored a convincing win in the resulting <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Eckm%C3%BChl" title="Battle of Eckmühl">Battle of Eckmühl</a>, forcing Charles to withdraw his forces over the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and into <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>. On 13 May, Vienna fell for the second time in four years, although the war continued since most of the Austrian army had survived the initial engagements in Southern Germany.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2486" data-file-width="5105" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg/220px-Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg/330px-Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg/440px-Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wigand-Entry_of_Napoleon_in_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The entry of Napoleon in <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn</a>, Vienna</div></div></div>
<p>On 21 May, the French made their first major effort to cross the Danube, precipitating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aspern-Essling" title="Battle of Aspern-Essling">Battle of Aspern-Essling</a>. The battle was characterized by a vicious back-and-forth struggle for the two villages of Aspern and Essling, the focal points of the French bridgehead. A sustained Austrian artillery bombardment eventually convinced Napoleon to withdraw his forces back onto Lobau Island. Both sides inflicted about 23,000 casualties on each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[174]</a></sup> It was the first defeat Napoleon suffered in a major set-piece battle, and it caused excitement throughout many parts of Europe because it proved that he could be beaten on the battlefield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[175]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the setback at Aspern-Essling, Napoleon took more than six weeks in planning and preparing for contingencies before he made another attempt at crossing the Danube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973708_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973708-184">[176]</a></sup> From 30 June to the early days of July, the French recrossed the Danube in strength, with more than 180,000 troops marching across the Marchfeld towards the Austrians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973708_184-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973708-184">[176]</a></sup> Charles received the French with 150,000 of his own men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973720_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973720-185">[177]</a></sup> In the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a>, which also lasted two days, Napoleon commanded his forces in what was the largest battle of his career up until then. Napoleon finished off the battle with a concentrated central thrust that punctured a hole in the Austrian army and forced Charles to retreat. Austrian losses were very heavy, reaching well over 40,000 casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973729_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973729-186">[178]</a></sup> The French were too exhausted to pursue the Austrians immediately, but Napoleon eventually caught up with Charles at <a href="/wiki/Znojmo" title="Znojmo">Znaim</a> and the latter signed an <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Znaim" title="Armistice of Znaim">armistice</a> on 12 July.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_Empire_(1812).svg"><img alt="Map of Europe. French Empire shown as bigger than present day France as it included parts of present-day Netherlands and Italy." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/French_Empire_%281812%29.svg/220px-French_Empire_%281812%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/French_Empire_%281812%29.svg/330px-French_Empire_%281812%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/French_Empire_%281812%29.svg/440px-French_Empire_%281812%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:French_Empire_(1812).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French Empire</a> at its greatest extent in 1812:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#008000; color:white;"> </span> French Empire</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#49C946; color:black;"> </span> French <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite states</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a>, the British launched the <a href="/wiki/Walcheren_Campaign" title="Walcheren Campaign">Walcheren Campaign</a> to open up a second front in the war and to relieve the pressure on the Austrians. The British army only landed at <a href="/wiki/Walcheren" title="Walcheren">Walcheren</a> on 30 July, by which point the Austrians had already been defeated. The Walcheren Campaign was characterized by little fighting but heavy casualties thanks to the popularly dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Walcheren" title="Walcheren">Walcheren Fever</a>". Over 4,000 British troops were lost in a bungled campaign, and the rest withdrew in December 1809.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[179]</a></sup> The main strategic result from the campaign became the delayed political settlement between the French and the Austrians. Emperor Francis wanted to wait and see how the British performed in their theatre before entering into negotiations with Napoleon. Once it became apparent that the British were going nowhere, the Austrians agreed to peace talks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn" title="Treaty of Schönbrunn">Treaty of Schönbrunn</a> in October 1809 was the harshest that France had imposed on Austria in recent memory. <a href="/wiki/Klemens_von_Metternich" title="Klemens von Metternich">Metternich</a> and Archduke Charles had the preservation of the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Habsburg Empire</a> as their fundamental goal, and to this end, they succeeded by making Napoleon seek more modest goals in return for promises of friendship between the two powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Todd_Fisher_p._144_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Todd_Fisher_p._144-188">[180]</a></sup> Nevertheless, while most of the hereditary lands remained a part of the Habsburg realm, France received <a href="/wiki/Carinthia_(Slovenia)" title="Carinthia (Slovenia)">Carinthia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carniola" title="Carniola">Carniola</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> ports, while <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a> was given to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw" title="Duchy of Warsaw">Poles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a> area of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a> went to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Bavarians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Todd_Fisher_p._144_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-Todd_Fisher_p._144-188">[180]</a></sup> Austria lost over three million subjects, about one-fifth of her total population, as a result of these territorial changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler1973732_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler1973732-189">[181]</a></sup> Although fighting in Iberia continued, the War of the Fifth Coalition would be the last major conflict on the European continent for the next three years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Napoleon turned his focus to domestic affairs after the war. <a href="/wiki/Empress_Jos%C3%A9phine" title="Empress Joséphine">Empress Joséphine</a> had still not given birth to a child from Napoleon, who became worried about the future of his empire following his death. Desperate for a legitimate heir, Napoleon divorced Joséphine on 10 January 1810 and started looking for a new wife. Hoping to cement the recent alliance with Austria through a family connection, Napoleon married the <a href="/wiki/Marie_Louise,_Duchess_of_Parma" title="Marie Louise, Duchess of Parma">Marie Louise, Duchess of Parma</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Francis_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis II, Holy Roman Emperor">Francis II</a>, who was 18 years old at the time. On 20 March 1811, Marie Louise gave birth to a baby boy, whom Napoleon made heir apparent and bestowed the title of <i><a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans#First_French_Empire" title="King of the Romans">King of Rome</a></i>. His son never actually ruled the empire, but given his brief titular rule and cousin Louis-Napoléon's subsequent naming himself Napoléon III, historians often refer to him as <i><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_II" title="Napoleon II">Napoleon II</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_of_Russia">Invasion of Russia</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">French invasion of Russia</a></div>
<p>In 1808, Napoleon and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Tsar Alexander</a> met at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> to preserve the Russo-French alliance. The leaders had a friendly personal relationship after their first meeting at Tilsit in 1807.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[183]</a></sup> By 1811, however, tensions had increased and Alexander was under pressure from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_nobility" title="Russian nobility">Russian nobility</a> to break off the alliance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A major strain on the relationship between the two nations became the regular violations of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_System" title="Continental System">Continental System</a> by the Russians as their economy was failing, which led Napoleon to threaten Alexander with serious consequences if he formed an alliance with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[184]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_(1841).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1968" data-file-width="2612" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg/220px-Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg/330px-Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg/440px-Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_%281841%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_in_burning_Moscow_-_Adam_Albrecht_(1841).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon watching the <a href="/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_(1812)" title="Fire of Moscow (1812)">fire of Moscow</a> in September 1812, by <a href="/wiki/Ada_Albrecht" title="Ada Albrecht">Adam Albrecht</a> (1841)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="762" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/220px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/330px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/440px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Napoleon's withdrawal from Russia</i>, painting by <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Northen" title="Adolph Northen">Adolph Northen</a></div></div></div>
<p>By 1812, advisers to Alexander suggested the possibility of an invasion of the French Empire and the recapture of Poland. On receipt of intelligence reports on Russia's war preparations, Napoleon expanded his <i>Grande Armée</i> to more than 450,000 men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[185]</a></sup> He ignored repeated advice against an invasion of the Russian heartland and prepared for an offensive campaign; on 24 June 1812 the invasion commenced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>In an attempt to gain increased support from Polish nationalists and patriots, Napoleon termed the war the <i>Second Polish War</i>—the <i>First Polish War</i> had been the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Confederation" title="Bar Confederation">Bar Confederation</a> uprising by Polish nobles against Russia in 1768. Polish patriots wanted the Russian part of Poland to be joined with the Duchy of Warsaw and an independent Poland created. This was rejected by Napoleon, who stated he had promised his ally Austria this would not happen.
